     662              : // Presence of language & library features:
     663              : 
     664              : #if gsl_COMPILER_CLANG_VERSION || gsl_COMPILER_APPLECLANG_VERSION
     665              : # ifdef __OBJC__
     666              :    // There are a bunch of inconsistencies about __EXCEPTIONS and __has_feature(cxx_exceptions) in Clang 3.4/3.5/3.6.
     667              :    // We're interested in C++ exceptions, which can be checked by __has_feature(cxx_exceptions) in 3.5+.
     668              :    // In pre-3.5, __has_feature(cxx_exceptions) can be true if ObjC exceptions are enabled, but C++ exceptions are disabled.
     669              :    // The recommended way to check is `__EXCEPTIONS && __has_feature(cxx_exceptions)`.
     670              :    // See https://releases.llvm.org/3.6.0/tools/clang/docs/ReleaseNotes.html#the-exceptions-macro
     671              :    // Note: this is only relevant in Objective-C++, thus the ifdef.
     672              : #  if __EXCEPTIONS && __has_feature(cxx_exceptions)
     673              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  1
     674              : #  else
     675              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  0
     676              : #  endif // __EXCEPTIONS && __has_feature(cxx_exceptions)
     677              : # else
     678              :    // clang-cl doesn't define __EXCEPTIONS for MSVC compatibility (see https://reviews.llvm.org/D4065).
     679              :    // Neither does Clang in MS-compatiblity mode.
     680              :    // Let's hope no one tries to build Objective-C++ code using MS-compatibility mode or clang-cl.
     681              : #  if __has_feature(cxx_exceptions)
     682              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  1
     683              : #  else
     684              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  0
     685              : #  endif
     686              : # endif
     687              : #elif defined( __GNUC__ )
     688              : # if __GNUC__ < 5
     689              : #  ifdef __EXCEPTIONS
     690              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  1
     691              : #  else
     692              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  0
     693              : #  endif // __EXCEPTIONS
     694              : # else
     695              : #  ifdef __cpp_exceptions
     696              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  1
     697              : #  else
     698              : #   define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  0
     699              : #  endif // __cpp_exceptions
     700              : # endif // __GNUC__ < 5
     701              : #elif gsl_COMPILER_MSVC_VERSION
     702              : # ifdef _CPPUNWIND
     703              : #  define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  1
     704              : # else
     705              : #  define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  0
     706              : # endif // _CPPUNWIND
     707              : #else
     708              : // For all other compilers, assume exceptions are always enabled.
     709              : # define  gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS  1
     710              : #endif
     711              : #define gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS_()  gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS
     712              : 
     713              : #if defined( gsl_CONFIG_CONTRACT_VIOLATION_THROWS ) && ! gsl_HAVE_EXCEPTIONS
     714              : # error Cannot use gsl_CONFIG_CONTRACT_VIOLATION_THROWS if exceptions are disabled.
     715              : #endif // defined( gsl_CONFIG_CONTRACT_VIOLATION_THROWS ) && !gsl_HAVE( EXCEPTIONS )

    1164              : // GSL API (e.g. for CUDA platform):
    1165              : 
    1166              : // Guidelines for using `gsl_api`:
    1167              : //
    1168              : // NVCC imposes the restriction that a function annotated `__host__ __device__` cannot call host-only or device-only functions.
    1169              : // This makes `gsl_api` inappropriate for generic functions that call unknown code, e.g. the template constructors of `span<>`
    1170              : // or functions like `finally()` which accept an arbitrary  function object.
    1171              : // It is often preferable to annotate functions only with `gsl_constexpr` or `gsl_constexpr14`. The "extended constexpr" mode
    1172              : // of NVCC (currently an experimental feature) will implicitly consider constexpr functions `__host__ __device__` functions
    1173              : // but tolerates calls to host-only or device-only functions.
    1174              : 
    1175              : #ifndef   gsl_api
    1176              : # ifdef   __CUDACC__
    1177              : #  define gsl_api __host__ __device__
    1178              : # else
    1179              : #  define gsl_api /*gsl_api*/
    1180              : # endif
    1181              : #endif

    1277              : // - C26432: gsl::c.21  : if you define or delete any default operation in the type '...', define or delete them all
    1278              : // - C26410: gsl::r.32  : the parameter 'ptr' is a reference to const unique pointer, use const T* or const T& instead
    1279              : // - C26415: gsl::r.30  : smart pointer parameter 'ptr' is used only to access contained pointer. Use T* or T& instead
    1280              : // - C26418: gsl::r.36  : shared pointer parameter 'ptr' is not copied or moved. Use T* or T& instead
    1281              : // - C26472: gsl::t.1   : don't use a static_cast for arithmetic conversions;
    1282              : //                        use brace initialization, gsl::narrow_cast or gsl::narrow
    1283              : // - C26439: gsl::f.6   : special function 'function' can be declared 'noexcept'
    1284              : // - C26440: gsl::f.6   : function 'function' can be declared 'noexcept'
    1285              : // - C26455: gsl::f.6   : default constructor may not throw. Declare it 'noexcept'
    1286              : // - C26473: gsl::t.1   : don't cast between pointer types where the source type and the target type are the same
    1287              : // - C26481: gsl::b.1   : don't use pointer arithmetic. Use span instead
    1288              : // - C26482: gsl::b.2   : only index into arrays using constant expressions
    1289              : // - C26446: gdl::b.4   : prefer to use gsl::at() instead of unchecked subscript operator
    1290              : // - C26490: gsl::t.1   : don't use reinterpret_cast
    1291              : // - C26487: gsl::l.4   : don't return a pointer '(<some number>'s result)' that may be invalid
    1292              : // - C26434: gsl::c.128 : function 'symbol_1' hides a non-virtual function 'symbol_2' (false positive for compiler-generated functions such as constructors)
    1293              : // - C26456: gsl::c.128 : operator 'symbol_1' hides a non-virtual operator 'symbol_2' (false positive for compiler-generated operators)
    1294              : // - C26457: es.48      : (void) should not be used to ignore return values, use 'std::ignore =' instead

    1311              : // C++98 emulation:
    1312              : 
    1313              : namespace detail {
    1314              : 
    1315              : // We implement `equal()` and `lexicographical_compare()` here to avoid having to pull in the <algorithm> header.
    1316              : template< class InputIt1, class InputIt2 >
    1317              : bool equal( InputIt1 first1, InputIt1 last1, InputIt2 first2 )
    1318              : {
    1319              :     // Implementation borrowed from https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/algorithm/equal.
    1320              :     for ( ; first1 != last1; ++first1, ++first2 )
    1321              :     {
    1322              :         if ( ! (*first1 == *first2 ) ) return false;
    1323              :     }
    1324              :     return true;
    1325              : }
    1326              : template< class InputIt1, class InputIt2 >
    1327              : bool lexicographical_compare( InputIt1 first1, InputIt1 last1, InputIt2 first2, InputIt2 last2 )
    1328              : {
    1329              :     // Implementation borrowed from https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/algorithm/lexicographical_compare.
    1330              :     for ( ; first1 != last1 && first2 != last2; ++first1, static_cast< void >( ++first2 ) )
    1331              :     {
    1332              :         if ( *first1 < *first2 ) return true;
    1333              :         if ( *first2 < *first1 ) return false;
    1334              :     }
    1335              :     return first1 == last1 && first2 != last2;
    1336              : }
    1337              : 
    1338              : } // namespace detail

    2136              : class final_action
    2137              : {
    2138              : public:
    2139              :     explicit final_action( F action ) gsl_noexcept
    2140              :         : action_( std::move( action ) )
    2141              : #if gsl_CONFIG_DEFAULTS_VERSION < 1 || ! gsl_CPP17_OR_GREATER
    2142              :         , invoke_( true )

    2144              :     {
    2145              :     }

    2164              :         if ( invoke_ )
    2165              : #endif

    2187              : };

    2521              :

    3081              : 
    3082              :     // We want an implicit conversion operator that can be used to convert from both lvalues (by
    3083              :     // const reference or by copy) and rvalues (by move). So it seems like we could define
    3084              :     //
    3085              :     //     template< class U >
    3086              :     //     operator U const &() const & { ... }
    3087              :     //     template< class U >
    3088              :     //     operator U &&() && { ... }
    3089              :     //
    3090              :     // However, having two conversion operators with different return types renders the assignment
    3091              :     // operator of the result type ambiguous:
    3092              :     //
    3093              :     //     not_null<std::unique_ptr<T>> p( ... );
    3094              :     //     std::unique_ptr<U> q;
    3095              :     //     q = std::move( p ); // ambiguous
    3096              :     //
    3097              :     // To avoid this ambiguity, we have both overloads of the conversion operator return `U`
    3098              :     // rather than `U const &` or `U &&`. This implies that converting an lvalue always induces
    3099              :     // a copy, which can cause unnecessary copies or even fail to compile in some situations:
    3100              :     //
    3101              :     //     not_null<std::shared_ptr<T>> sp( ... );
    3102              :     //     std::shared_ptr<U> const & rs = sp; // unnecessary copy
    3103              :     //     std::unique_ptr<U> const & ru = p; // error: cannot copy `unique_ptr<T>`
    3104              :     //
    3105              :     // However, these situations are rather unusual, and the following, more frequent situations
    3106              :     // remain unimpaired:
    3107              :     //
    3108              :     //     std::shared_ptr<U> vs = sp; // no extra copy
    3109              :     //     std::unique_ptr<U> vu = std::move( p );
    3110              : 
    3111              : #if gsl_HAVE( MOVE_FORWARD ) && gsl_HAVE( TYPE_TRAITS ) && gsl_HAVE( DEFAULT_FUNCTION_TEMPLATE_ARG ) && gsl_HAVE( EXPLICIT )
    3112              :     // explicit conversion operator
    3113              : 
    3114              :     template< class U
    3115              :         // We *have* to use SFINAE with an NTTP arg here, otherwise the overload is ambiguous.
    3116              :         , typename std::enable_if< ( std::is_constructible<U, T const &>::value && !std::is_convertible<T, U>::value && !detail::is_not_null_or_bool_oracle<U>::value ), int >::type = 0
    3117              :     >
    3118              :     gsl_NODISCARD gsl_api gsl_constexpr14 explicit
    3119              :     operator U() const
    3120              : # if gsl_HAVE( FUNCTION_REF_QUALIFIER )
    3121              :     &
    3122              : # endif
    3123              :     {
    3124              :         return U( accessor::get_checked( *this ) );

    3458              : 
    3459              : // The C++ Core Guidelines discourage the use of pointer arithmetic, and gsl-lite consequently refrains from defining operators
    3460              : // for pointer arithmetic or the subscript operator in `not_null<>`. However, comparison of `not_null<>` objects is supported;
    3461              : // although the standard does not mandate a certain ordering for objects with two exceptions (objects from the same array;
    3462              : // data members of the same class, as required for `offsetof()`), it does require that `operator<` establishes a total ordering
    3463              : // of pointers, as implied by https://eel.is/c++draft/expr.rel#5. Among other things, this guarantees that a list of pointers
    3464              : // can be sorted and searched, or that pointers can be used as a key in a relational container such as `std::map<>`.
    3465              : // Therefore, we also define relational comparison operators for `not_null<>`.
    3466              : 
    3467              : template< class T, class U >
    3468              : gsl_NODISCARD inline gsl_api gsl_constexpr gsl_TRAILING_RETURN_TYPE_( bool )
    3469              : operator<( not_null<T> const & l, not_null<U> const & r )
    3470              : gsl_RETURN_DECLTYPE_( l.operator->() < r.operator->() )
    3471              : {
    3472              :     return l.operator->() < r.operator->();
    3473              : }
    3474              : template< class T, class U >
    3475              : gsl_NODISCARD inline gsl_api gsl_constexpr gsl_TRAILING_RETURN_TYPE_( bool )

    4064              :     gsl_NODISCARD gsl_api gsl_constexpr14 span
    4065              :     subspan( index_type offset, index_type count ) const

    4556              : 
    4557              : template< class T >
    4558              : gsl_api inline gsl_constexpr14 std::size_t string_length( T * ptr, std::size_t max )
    4559              : {
    4560              :     if ( ptr == gsl_nullptr || max <= 0 )
    4561              :         return 0;
    4562              : 
    4563              :     std::size_t len = 0;
    4564              :     while ( len < max && ptr[len] ) // NOLINT
    4565              :         ++len;
    4566              : 
    4567              :     return len;
    4568              : }
    4569              : 
    4570              : } // namespace detail

    4572              : //
    4573              : // basic_string_span<> - A view of contiguous characters, replace (*,len).
    4574              : //
    4575              : template< class T >
    4576              : class basic_string_span
    4577              : {
    4578              : public:
    4579              :     typedef T element_type;
    4580              :     typedef span<T> span_type;
    4581              : 
    4582              :     typedef typename span_type::size_type size_type;
    4583              :     typedef typename span_type::index_type index_type;
    4584              :     typedef typename span_type::difference_type difference_type;
    4585              : 
    4586              :     typedef typename span_type::pointer pointer ;
    4587              :     typedef typename span_type::reference reference ;

    5265              : //
    5266              : // ensure_sentinel()
    5267              : //
    5268              : // Provides a way to obtain a span from a contiguous sequence
    5269              : // that ends with a (non-inclusive) sentinel value.
    5270              : //
    5271              : // Will fail-fast if sentinel cannot be found before max elements are examined.
    5272              : //
    5273              : namespace detail {
    5274              : 
    5275              : template< class T, class SizeType, const T Sentinel >
    5276              : gsl_constexpr14 static span<T> ensure_sentinel( T * seq, SizeType max = (std::numeric_limits<SizeType>::max)() )
    5277              : {
    5278              :     typedef T * pointer;
    5279              : 
    5280              :     gsl_SUPPRESS_MSVC_WARNING( 26429, "f.23: symbol 'cur' is never tested for nullness, it can be marked as not_null" )
    5281              :     pointer cur = seq;
    5282              : 
    5283              :     while ( static_cast<SizeType>( cur - seq ) < max && *cur != Sentinel )
    5284              :         ++cur;
    5285              : 
    5286              :     gsl_Expects( *cur == Sentinel );
    5287              : 
    5288              :     return span<T>( seq, gsl::narrow_cast< typename span<T>::index_type >( cur - seq ) );
    5289              : }
    5290              : } // namespace detail
    5291              : 
    5292              : //
    5293              : // ensure_z - creates a string_span for a czstring or cwzstring.
    5294              : // Will fail fast if a null-terminator cannot be found before
    5295              : // the limit of size_type.
    5296              : //
    5297              : 
    5298              : template< class T >
    5299              : gsl_NODISCARD inline gsl_constexpr14 span<T>
    5300              : ensure_z( T * const & sz, size_t max = (std::numeric_limits<size_t>::max)() )
    5301              : {
    5302              :     return detail::ensure_sentinel<T, size_t, 0>( sz, max );
    5303              : }
    5304              : 
    5305              : template< class T, size_t N >
    5306              : gsl_NODISCARD inline gsl_constexpr14 span<T>
    5307              : ensure_z( T (&sz)[N] )
    5308              : {
    5309              :     return ::gsl::ensure_z( gsl_ADDRESSOF( sz[0] ), N );
    5310              : }
    5311              :

    5489              : #if gsl_FEATURE( GSL_LITE_NAMESPACE )
    5490              : 
    5491              : // gsl_lite namespace:
    5492              : 
    5493              : // gsl-lite currently keeps all symbols in the namespace `gsl`. The `gsl_lite` namespace contains all the symbols in the
    5494              : // `gsl` namespace, plus some extensions that are not specified in the Core Guidelines.
    5495              : //
    5496              : // Going forward, we want to support coexistence of gsl-lite with M-GSL, so we want to encourage using the `gsl_lite`
    5497              : // namespace when consuming gsl-lite. Typical use in library code would be:
    5498              : //
    5499              : //     #include <gsl-lite/gsl-lite.hpp>  // instead of <gsl/gsl-lite.hpp>
    5500              : //
    5501              : //     namespace foo {
    5502              : //         namespace gsl = ::gsl_lite;  // convenience alias
    5503              : //         double mean( gsl::span<double const> elements )
    5504              : //         {
    5505              : //             gsl_Expects( ! elements.empty() );  // instead of Expects()
    5506              : //             ...
    5507              : //         }
    5508              : //     } // namespace foo
    5509              : //
    5510              : // In a future version, the new <gsl-lite/gsl-lite.hpp> header will only define the `gsl_lite` namespace and no
    5511              : // unprefixed `Expects()` and `Ensures()` macros to avoid collision with M-GSL. To ensure backward compatibility, the
    5512              : // old header <gsl/gsl-lite.hpp> will keep defining the `gsl` namespace and the `Expects()` and `Ensures()` macros.
    5513              : 
    5514              : namespace gsl_lite {
    5515              : 
    5516              : namespace std11 = ::gsl::std11;
    5517              : namespace std14 = ::gsl::std14;
    5518              : namespace std17 = ::gsl::std17;
    5519              : namespace std20 = ::gsl::std20;
    5520              : namespace std23 = ::gsl::std23;
    5521              : 
    5522              : using namespace std11;
    5523              : //using namespace std14;  // contains only make_unique<>(), which is superseded by `gsl::make_unique<>()`
    5524              : using namespace std17;
    5525              : using namespace std20;
    5526              : using namespace std23;
    5527              : 
    5528              : using namespace ::gsl::detail::no_adl;
    5529              : 
    5530              : # if gsl_HAVE( UNIQUE_PTR ) && gsl_HAVE( SHARED_PTR )
    5531              : using std::unique_ptr;
    5532              : using std::shared_ptr;
    5533              : #  if gsl_HAVE( VARIADIC_TEMPLATE )
    5534              : using ::gsl::make_unique;
    5535              : using ::gsl::make_shared;
    5536              : #  endif
    5537              : # endif
    5538              : 
    5539              : using ::gsl::index;
    5540              : using ::gsl::dim;

    5542              : using ::gsl::diff;
    5543              : 
    5544              : # if gsl_HAVE( ALIAS_TEMPLATE )

    5546              :   template< class T
